## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of velocity and time. Without explicit position, the formula likely involves nonlinear damping/restoring terms in velocity combined with time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear damping: dv_dt = c0 * v (simple viscous damping)
- Van der Pol damping: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v (amplitude-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Harmonic driving: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * t + c2) (sinusoidal external forcing)
- Damped driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (linear damping plus harmonic drive)
- Nonlinear damping with drive: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (van der Pol with forcing)
- Cubic restoring via velocity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 (polynomial nonlinearity in velocity)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v**5 (higher-order velocity terms)
- Parametric excitation: dv_dt = c0 * v * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated coefficient)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * v - c1 * v**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (Rayleigh with harmonic drive)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * v + c1 * v * Abs(v) (velocity-dependent quadratic drag)
- Mathieu-type: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * v (parametric oscillator)
- General polynomial with drive: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**2 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (general low-order expansion)
- Negative damping with saturation: dv_dt = c0 * v * (c1 - v**2) + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (self-sustained oscillation with forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ‚Üí Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ‚Üí Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ‚Üí Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ‚Üí Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ‚Üí Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Self-sustained oscillation (limit cycle) ‚Üí terms like (1 - v¬≤)*v indicating amplitude-dependent damping sign change
- Harmonic driving forces ‚Üí sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms appear additively when external periodic forcing is present
- Parametric resonance ‚Üí velocity multiplied by periodic time function v*cos(c*t) indicates time-varying stiffness/damping
- Odd-symmetry in velocity ‚Üí only odd powers of v (v, v¬≥, v‚Åµ) appear when the system has time-reversal or spatial symmetry
- Energy balance in steady state ‚Üí nonlinear damping terms must have both energy-injecting and energy-dissipating regions (sign changes in coefficient of v)
- Phase space reconstruction ‚Üí when position is absent, trigonometric functions of time may encode the implicit position dependence through x ~ sin(œât)
- Frequency locking in driven systems ‚Üí the driving frequency c*t in sin/cos relates to natural frequency through rational ratios
- Soft vs hard spring behavior ‚Üí sign of cubic term determines whether frequency increases (positive) or decreases (negative) with amplitude
